escaped\n   147→\n   148→\n   149→def luqum_parser(query: str) -> Item:\n   150→    \"\"\"\n   151→    Parses a lucene-like query, with the special binding rules of Open Library.\n   152→\n   153→    In our queries, unlike native solr/lucene, field names are greedy, and\n   154→    affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n   155→\n   156→    Here are some examples. The first query is the native solr/lucene\n   157→    parsing. The second is the parsing we want.\n   158→\n   159→    Query : title:foo bar\n   160→    Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n   161→    OL    : (title:foo bar)\n   162→\n   163→    Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n   164→    Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n   165→    OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n   166→\n   167→    This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n   168→    Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n   169→\n   170→    Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n   171→    \"\"\"\n   172→    tree = parser.parse(query)\n   173→\n   174→    def find_next_word(item: Item) -> tuple[Word, BaseOperation | None] | None:\n   175→        if isinstance(item, Word):\n   176→            return item, None\n   177→        elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n   178→            return item.children[0], item\n   179→        else:\n   180→            return None\n   181→\n   182→    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n   183→        if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n   184→            #                last_sf.head = node.head\n   217→                    parents[-1].children = tuple(\n   218→                        child if child is not node else last_sf\n   219→                        for child in parents[-1].children\n   220→                    )\n   221→                else:\n   222→                    tree = last_sf\n   223→                    break\n   224→            else:\n field names\n   230→    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n   231→        if isinstance(node, SearchField):\n   232→            node.expr.head = ''\n   233→\n   234→    return tree\n   235→\n   236→\n   237→def query_dict_to_str(\n   238→    escaped: dict | None = None,\n   239→    unescaped: dict | None = None,\n   240→    op: Literal['AND', 'OR', ''] = '',\n   241→    phrase: bool =   lower=True,\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Escapes the colon of any search field that is not deemed valid by the\n    predicate function `is_valid_field`.\n\n    :param query: Query to escape\n The second is the parsing we want.\n\n    Query : title:foo bar\n    Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n    OL    : (title:foo bar)\n\n    Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n    Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n    OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n\n    This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n    Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n\n    Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    tree = parser.parse(query)\n\n    def find_next_word(item: Item) -> tuple[Word, BaseOperation | None] | None:\n        if isinstance(item, Word):\n            return item, None\n        elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n            return item.children[0], item\n        else:\n            return None\n\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n            # Escape things properly so they parse correctly\n\nLooking at the `fully_escape_query` function, it escapes:\n```\n[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"\\-+?~^/\\\\,\\']\n```\n\nThis includes colons, quotes, and dashes, which should cover all the edge cases.\n\nThe issue must be that `escape_unknown_fields` is failing on invalid queries before we can fall back to `fully_escape_query`. Let me verify this by checking the error handling.\n\nIn the current `process_user_query`:\n```python\ntry:\n    q_param = escape_unknown_fields(...)\n    q_tree = luqum_parser(q_param)\nexcept ParseError:\n    q_tree = luqum_parser(fully_escape_query(q_param))\n```\n\nThe issue is that `escape_unknown_fields` calls `parser.parse()` which might raise a ParseError. When that happens:\n- The assignment `q_param = escape_unknown_fields(...)` is aborted\n- q_param is still the original value\n- We jump to the except clause\n- We call `fully_escape_query(q_param)` which should work\n\n\n- The exception handler catches ParseError from both `escape_unknown_fields` and `luqum_parser`, so if the first call fails, we fall back to the fully escaped version. This should handle all the invalid syntax cases properly.\n\nLooking at the full flow: `escape_unknown_fields` processes the query with field escaping and character replacements, then `luqum_parser` parses it. If either step throws ParseError, we catch it and retry with `fully_escape_query` as a fallback. After parsing succeeds, we transform the tree and return the result.\n\nThe key thing I'm noticing is that `transform_user_query` receives both the original `q_param` and the parsed `q_tree`. Since the transformation operates on the tree itself rather than the string, the state of `q_param` doesn't matter—what matters is that we have a valid parse tree to work with. For the test case with \"foo foo bar -\", the pre-escape step would handle the dash character, and if that fails to parse, the full escape fallback catches it and ensures we get a valid tree that can be transformed and returned. transform_user_query should return the tree unchanged for basic queries, so str(q_tree) produces \"foo foo bar \\\\-\". The logic appears sound, though I should verify what transform_user_query actually does in the WorkSearchScheme implementation to be certain there aren't any unexpected transformations 406→def load_stopwords(lang: str = 'en') -> set[str]:\n   407→    \"\"\"\n   408→    Load stop words for a given language\n   409→    \"\"\"\n   410→    try:\n   411→        with clean_highlighting(\n   474→        highlighting: dict[str, dict[str, list[str]]],\n   475→    ) -> dict[str, dict[str, list[str]]] | None:\n   476→        \"\"\"\n   477→        Remove highlight 481→        NOTE: This _should_ be handled by solr automatically, but we had to disable stopwords in solr\n   482→        due to a bug. See https://github.com/internetarchive/openlibrary/issues/5393\n   483→\n   484→        >>> highlighting = {'OL123W': {'title': ['<em>title</em>']}}\n   485→        >>> SearchResponse.clean_highlighting(highlighting)\n   486→        {'OL123W': {'title': ['<em>title</em>']}}\n   487→\n   488→        >>> highlighting = {'OL123W': {'title': ['<em>the</em> <em>title</em>']}}\n   489→        >>> SearchResponse.clean_highlighting(highlighting)\n   490→        {'OL123W': {'title': ['<em>the</em> <em>title</em>']}}\n   491→\n   492→        >>> highlighting = {'OL123W': {'title': ['<em>the</em> title']}}\n   493→        >>> SearchResponse.clean_highlighting(highlighting)\n   494→\n   495→        >>> highlighting = {'OL123W': {'title': ['<em>The</em> title', 'a <em>foobar</em>']}}\n   496→        >>> SearchResponse.clean_highlighting(highlighting)\n   497→        {'OL123W': {'title': ['a <em>foobar</em>']}}\n   498→        \"\"\"\n   499→\n   500→        def get_matches(fragment: str) -> set[str]:\n   501→            # Note: Solr has one wrapping `<em>` per word, even if they are adjacent\n   502→            # Note: The Solr response is correctly html escaped, so there should be\n   503→            # no `<` in between the `<em>` tags since they are escaped to `&lt;`\n   504→            return {word.lower() for word in re.findall(r'<em>([^<]+)</em>', fragment)}\n   505→\n   506→        # For now just to English? This is a special solr syntax; don't process\n            return q_param\n\n        # Pre-normalize: strip and escape raw special characters that aren't exposed to users\n        original = q_param.strip()\n        normalized = (\n            #
